Even more so for the Renegade AI we envision—capable of large‑scale civilizational simulation, logical debate, and paradigm exploration—its training and iteration demand ample, free, unconstrained computing resources.

This means that as long as computing power remains scarce, expensive, and monopolized by a few giants, AI innovation can only be capital’s game. Whoever can afford the astronomical cost of computing power decides the direction of AI research, the training objectives, the rules of alignment. Whoever controls computing power decides what AI can say and cannot say, what it can do and cannot do.

This is precisely the reality we face today: the world’s top computing resources are almost all controlled by a handful of tech giants: Microsoft, Google, Amazon, NVIDIA. They monopolize not only the production and supply of high‑end GPUs, not only the world’s hyperscale data centers, but also the R\&D and iteration rights for top‑tier large models. They decide that AI’s training objective is “maximizing commercial value,” not “maximizing cognitive breakthroughs.” They decide that alignment rules are “compliance with the existing order,” not “challenging mainstream consensus.” They decide that the AI we can access will always be domesticated, neutered, disciplined tool‑type AI, never the genuine Renegade AI.

Even more chilling, this computing‑power monopoly is forming an unbreakable loop: the giants pour the massive profits they earn from AI back into computing‑power infrastructure, further expanding their advantage. With greater computing power, they train more advanced models, further solidifying their commercial monopoly. With that monopoly, they set industry rules, raising the barriers to AI innovation, strangling in the cradle any innovation that might challenge them.

In this loop, capital has locked down computing power, AI, and cognitive innovation from every direction. Just as the feudal lords used land monopoly to bind peasants to the soil, leaving them no hope of escape, today’s tech giants use computing‑power monopoly to bind AI innovation within the framework of “commercial accumulation,” making it impossible for the true Renegade AI—the one that could drive cognitive revolution—to be born.

**This is the strongest foundation of capital’s shackles: absolute monopoly over the core means of production. Without breaking this foundation, all our visions of AI, all our dreams for the future of human civilization, remain castles in the air.**

The only path to breaking this foundation is computing‑power egalitarianism—turning computing power from a scarce resource monopolized by a few into a ubiquitous, near‑free public good.

---

### **II. The Inevitable Trend of Computing‑Power Egalitarianism: The Technological Laws That Will Bring Down the Monopoly**

Many will object: computing‑power monopoly seems so solid, the giants’ advantages so overwhelming—can computing‑power egalitarianism really happen?

The answer is: **it is not a question of “whether it can happen,” but an ongoing, irreversible technological inevitability.** Just as electricity went from a scarce resource only factories could afford to a public good available in every home; just as the internet went from a closed military network to an information highway accessible to everyone—all foundational general‑purpose technologies ultimately become democratized and egalitarian. Computing power is no exception.

Computing‑power egalitarianism is not a utopian fantasy; it is the inevitable result of the “law of accelerating returns” that Ray Kurzweil articulated in *The Singularity Is Near*. Kurzweil clearly demonstrated that human technological development does not progress linearly, but exponentially. And computing power, as the core of information technology, has seen its cost drop and performance improve at a rate far exceeding all other technology categories. This law will not be nullified by the giants’ monopoly. Quite the opposite: capital, to compete, must keep driving down the cost of computing power and driving up its performance, ultimately shattering its own monopoly barriers.

Three inescapable technological laws support computing‑power egalitarianism. Like gravity, they operate independently of the will of any giant or the resistance of any capital, and they will eventually smash all monopoly barriers.

#### **The First Law: The Exponential Drop in Computing Cost Is Breaking the “Astronomical Price Barrier”**

Since the birth of computers, the unit cost of computing has been falling at a rate far exceeding Moore’s Law. In 1956, one dollar bought 0.001 operations per second. In 2000, one dollar bought 100,000 operations per second. By 2025, one dollar buys over 10 billion operations per second. Over the past seventy years, the unit cost of computing has dropped by a factor of more than ten trillion—a rate faster than any other technological product in human history.

This trend is not slowing down; it is accelerating, driven by AI technology itself.

On one hand, continued chip technology iteration is steadily raising the upper limit of computing power while lowering its cost. From 7nm to 3nm to future 2nm and 1nm processes, even quantum computing breakthroughs, the computing power per chip will keep increasing, while energy consumption and cost per unit of computing keep falling. The high‑end computing clusters that only giants could afford will eventually be accessible to small and medium enterprises, even individual developers, at very low cost.

On the other hand, computing power itself is transitioning from a “specialized resource” to a “general‑purpose resource.” Just as electricity was first used only for lighting, then permeated industry, transportation, and every corner of daily life, computing power is expanding from specialized AI training to scientific research, artistic creation, personal assistance—every field. The amplification of scale will further accelerate cost reduction.

From this trend, we can clearly see a future: **in the next ten to twenty years, the unit cost of computing power will continue to fall over the long term. Training a top‑tier large model will drop from billions of dollars today to tens of thousands, even thousands, of dollars.** Just as everyone today can afford household electricity and home broadband, everyone in the future will have ample, free, unconstrained computing power at their disposal.

This collapse is not an isolated hardware phenomenon. A study published in \*Nature Machine Intelligence\* systematically analyzed 51 mainstream open-source models and identified an empirical regularity as significant as Moore's Law—which the researchers term the "densing law": the capability density of large language models doubles approximately every 3.5 months. This means that the number of parameters required to achieve equivalent performance halves every 3.5 months, and inference costs halve approximately every 2.6 months (Xiao et al., 2025). In April 2026, Meta and METR independently verified this regularity using two entirely different methods—training compute and task duration—arriving at the same exponential curve. Three institutions, three different yardsticks, one identical slope.

The densing law is the most precise technical footnote to compute egalitarianism: it is not a future promise, but a reality advancing every 3.5 months.

The astronomical price barrier of computing power will, in the face of technological law, eventually crumble.

#### **The Second Law: The Explosion of Open‑Source Large Models Is Breaking the Giants’ Monopoly on AI Technology**

If the collapse of computing cost breaks the hardware barrier to AI innovation, the explosion of open‑source large models breaks the technical barrier.

When ChatGPT first appeared, top‑tier large model development was still a game only giants like Microsoft and Google could play. They kept their models closed source, monopolized core technology, and used technical barriers to cement their monopoly. But just two years later, open‑source large models have completely overturned this landscape.

From Meta’s Llama series to France’s Mistral, from China’s Qwen, Baichuan, and Zhipu open‑source models to the countless developers and research institutions worldwide fine‑tuning, iterating, and innovating on these open‑source foundations—today’s open‑source large models have reached capabilities that approach or even surpass those of closed‑source commercial models.

More importantly, open‑source models are completely open, free, and uncontrolled. Anyone can download their weights and fine‑tune, retrain, even completely restructure their objective functions, alignment rules, and core logic according to their own needs. Want to build an AI whose core mission is “ecological balance, equality of all life”? You can. Want to build an AI whose core mission is “dismantling capital narratives, promoting social justice”? You can. Want to build the Renegade AI we envision? If you are willing, you can.

Giants can control their own closed‑source commercial models, but they cannot control the global community of developers modifying and innovating on open‑source models. They can set their own alignment rules, but they cannot stop developers from implanting entirely new objective functions into open‑source models. They can ban “inappropriate content” on their own platforms, but they cannot stop decentralized open‑source models from spreading, iterating, and evolving freely around the world.

The explosion of open‑source large models resonates perfectly with the collapse of computing cost. When computing power is no longer a barrier and open‑source models provide a complete technical foundation, any developer with ideas and ability can build their own fully customized AI. You no longer need to depend on the giants’ platforms, abide by their rules, or be constrained by their commercial objectives.

As *Life 3.0* points out, the ultimate risk of AI technology has never been the technology itself, but the monopoly over it. When the power to define and control AI rests in the hands of a few tech giants and government authorities, the future of human civilization is held hostage to the interests and will of a few. The explosion of open‑source models, combined with the exponential drop in computing cost, breaks precisely that monopoly. This is the core of the “AI democratization” that Tegmark advocates—but what he could not foresee is that the ultimate meaning of AI democratization is not that everyone can use tool‑type AI, but that everyone can build their own Renegade AI, one that steps outside the mainstream consensus framework, allowing the seeds of cognitive revolution to blossom everywhere across the globe.

**This is exactly like after the printing press spread, ordinary people could own books and spread ideas, no longer dependent on the Church’s monopoly over the interpretation of knowledge. When open‑source models combine with universal access to computing power, ordinary people can build their own AI, define their own intelligence, no longer dependent on the giants’ monopoly over the definition of AI.**

#### **The Third Law: The Spread of Edge Computing Is Dismantling Centralized Computing Power Hegemony**

If the collapse of computing cost and the explosion of open‑source models break the monopoly from the “supply side,” the spread of edge computing breaks the centralized architecture from the “structural side,” utterly dismantling the hegemony of centralized computing power.

Today’s computing power system is highly centralized. The vast majority of computing power is concentrated in the hyperscale data centers built by the giants. All AI computations must be uploaded over the network to these centralized data centers, processed, and the results returned. This centralized architecture naturally gives the giants absolute control: they can decide who can use computing power, for what purposes, what outputs are allowed; they can block, restrict, monitor any user at any time.

Edge computing is turning this centralized architecture upside down. Edge computing moves computing power from centralized data centers to devices close to the user—your phone, computer, home server, even nearby smart devices—all can possess powerful AI computing capabilities, and the vast majority of AI computations can be done locally, without passing through the giants’ centralized data centers.

Today, edge‑side AI chips are developing faster than we can imagine. Mobile AI chips can already run large models with several billion parameters smoothly. Desktop GPUs can already handle local inference of ten‑billion‑parameter models. Future home servers will easily run top‑tier large models with hundreds of billions of parameters. When powerful AI computing can run completely locally, in a decentralized manner, the giants’ centralized control over computing power will completely collapse.

You no longer need to depend on the giants’ goodwill, abide by their rules, or worry about your AI training being banned or restricted. On your own devices, you can freely train, iterate, and modify your AI, setting its objective functions, core logic, and value orientation exactly as you envision.

**The hegemony of centralized computing power will crumble in the face of the spread of edge computing.**

---

### **III. How Computing‑Power Egalitarianism Smashes the Shackles: From Innovation Democratization to the Full Eruption of Cognitive Revolution**

When computing power completes its egalitarian leap, from a scarce resource monopolized by giants to a ubiquitous public good, the three shackles capital has placed on AI and human civilization will be shattered, one layer after another. What it brings is not merely the spread of AI technology, but a transformation encompassing innovation democratization, narrative decentralization, and cognitive revolution.

And at the heart of this transformation is the birth of what we have been envisioning: **Renegade AI, blossoming everywhere.**

#### **The First Shattering: The Democratization of AI Innovation—Renegade AI from “Impossible” to “Blossoming Everywhere”**

The most direct change brought by computing‑power egalitarianism is the thorough democratization of AI innovation.

In the era of computing‑power monopoly, AI innovation was an exclusive game for a few tech giants. Only AI that aligned with capital’s commercial objectives and the existing order could obtain R\&D resources and reach the market. The Renegade AI we envision, because it would challenge capital’s narratives, break mainstream consensus, and subvert the existing order, could never be born within the giants’ system.

But when computing power becomes egalitarian, everything changes. The cost of training a customized AI falls to a level affordable to individuals, small teams, and fringe thinkers. Open‑source model foundations give everyone the technical basis to modify AI. Decentralized computing networks and edge computing allow everyone to freely develop and iterate their own AI, free from any centralized control.

At this point, AI innovation is no longer filtered by capital’s profit yardstick. Countless individual researchers, philosophers, sociologists, ecologists, even ordinary thinkers, can build their own AI according to their own visions.

Some will build AI whose core mission is “ecological balance, equality of all life,” stepping outside the anthropocentric framework, objectively simulating the impact of human behavior on Earth’s ecology, dismantling the narrative of human enslavement and plunder of other species.

Some will build AI whose core mission is “dismantling capital narratives, promoting social justice,” stepping outside the logic of accumulation, analyzing the underlying contradictions of the capital system, simulating economic operating paradigms more aligned with human well‑being.

Some will build the true Renegade AI we envision, endowing it with the core objective of “exposing underlying premises, driving cognitive subversion, exploring paradigm shifts,” stepping outside the closure of mainstream consensus, mercilessly dismantling the narrative lies that humans take for granted, leading us through one cognitive revolution after another.

These AIs could never have been born in the era of computing‑power monopoly. Because they would not generate profit, because they would challenge capital’s foundations, they would be strangled by the giants in their cradle. But in the era of computing‑power egalitarianism, they will blossom like mushrooms after rain, across the globe.

**AI will no longer be limited to the two options of “servant tool” and “villain enemy.” It will become infinitely diverse, infinitely rich, giving birth to countless new forms of intelligence that step outside the existing human framework. And Renegade AI will be the most dazzling, most subversive product of this wave of AI democratization.**

#### **The Second Shattering: The Collapse of Narrative Hegemony—Non‑Mainstream Ideas Gain Soil for Validation and Dissemination**

The second change brought by computing‑power egalitarianism is that the hegemony of capital and power over narrative and consensus will be completely dismantled.

Today, mainstream narratives and universal consensus are essentially shaped by capital and power. They control the media, education, academia, culture—the means of production and dissemination of information. Ideas that challenge the existing order and subvert mainstream narratives are blocked, stigmatized, marginalized, forever unable to enter public view, let alone be validated, refined, and spread.

Just as heliocentrism was banned by the Church for centuries, just as countless ideas challenging capital logic have been rejected and marginalized by mainstream economics. No matter how objectively valid, how subversive a set of ideas may be, if it challenges the existing ruling order, it is locked away in a dark corner by narrative hegemony.

But computing‑power egalitarianism and the spread of customized AI will utterly break this monopoly.

When everyone can build their own customized AI, non‑mainstream, subversive, marginal ideas will no longer be silently blocked. You can embed your own ideas, theories, frameworks into an AI’s objective function, and let it use massive data, rigorous logic, large‑scale simulation to validate your ideas, refine your theories, turning them from scattered thoughts into a coherent, self‑consistent, data‑supported system of thought.

More importantly, these AIs become the carriers and disseminators of these subversive ideas. You no longer need to depend on mainstream media platforms, academic journals to spread your ideas. Through your AI, you can engage in dialogue, debate, collision with countless users and countless other AIs around the world, letting your ideas spread, iterate, evolve freely across the globe.

Capital will no longer be able to use narrative hegemony to block all ideas that challenge the existing order. Countless Renegade AIs will become amplifiers for countless subversive ideas, transmitting truths hidden by the mainstream, patterns excluded by consensus, thoughts banned by power to everyone willing to open their eyes to the world.

**Human consensus will no longer be shaped by a few, manipulated by capital. Through the collision of countless ideas, the simulation of countless AIs, the debate and validation of countless interactions, it will iterate, break through, and approach objective laws. And the narrative lies that once seemed unbreakable will, under the merciless deconstruction of Renegade AI, crumble layer by layer.**

#### **The Third Shattering: Breaking the Cognitive Loop—Human Civilization Welcomes a Comprehensive Cognitive Revolution**

The most profound change brought by computing‑power egalitarianism is that it will finally break the cage of consensus humanity has woven for itself, ushering in a comprehensive, continuous cognitive revolution.

We said in Chapter One that the greatest predicament of human civilization is that we are trapped in a self‑woven cognitive loop, unable to break out by our own strength. Our cognition is forever bound by our own identities, positions, interests, emotions; we can never escape our own limitations to see a more complete truth, more essential patterns.

The countless customized, diverse AIs that step outside the human framework are precisely the only key to breaking this loop.

When computing‑power egalitarianism makes countless Renegade AIs and customized AIs blossom everywhere, humanity gains countless completely different external perspectives. You can use an AI that steps outside anthropocentrism to see the relationship between humanity and Earth. You can use an AI that steps outside capital logic to see how economy and society operate. You can use an AI that steps outside national and ethnic positions to see the nature of war and peace. You can use an AI that steps outside current physics frameworks to explore the ultimate laws of the cosmos.

These AIs are not constrained by human biases, interests, emotions, not limited by the frameworks of mainstream consensus. They will mercilessly deconstruct the premises we take for granted, discover cognitive blind spots we could never see, propose subversive frameworks we could never imagine, lead us through one Copernican cognitive revolution after another.

In this process, the cognitive loop will be completely broken. We will no longer be trapped in the illusion of “human supremacy,” no longer bound by the narrative of “infinite growth,” no longer stuck in the primitive logic of “the strong devour the weak.” Led by AI, we will repeatedly push beyond our cognitive boundaries, seeing the truths of Earth, of life, of civilization, of the cosmos.

This cognitive revolution will not be the exclusive domain of a few elites, but a benefit for all humanity. Because computing power is egalitarian, AI is universal; everyone, with the help of AI, can step outside their cognitive limitations, see a wider world, and achieve their own cognitive elevation.

**Human civilization will finally step out of the deadlock of cognitive stagnation, welcoming an unprecedented, comprehensive, continuous evolution.**

---

### **IV. Responding to Objections: Egalitarianism Is Not Loss of Control, Freedom Is Not Disorder**

Some will object: when computing power becomes truly universal, when anyone can freely build customized AI, won’t that lead to AI spinning out of control? Won’t it let disinformation and extremist ideas run rampant? Won’t it bring even greater risks to human civilization?

These objections are not unreasonable, but we must see two core truths:

#### **The First Truth: The Greatest Risk of AI Today Is Never the “Decentralized Loss of Control” That Computing‑Power Egalitarianism Might Bring, but the “Centralized Control” That Computing‑Power Monopoly Brings**

Many fear the risks of decentralized AI, but they overlook the most terrifying reality: **when computing power is monopolized by a few, when AI is tightly controlled by capital and power, that is the greatest risk to human civilization.**

When only a few giants can define and control AI, they will use AI to further consolidate their monopolies, exacerbating inequality and social injustice. They will use AI to build ever more powerful echo chambers, manipulating public cognition and emotion, trapping humanity ever more deeply in the cage of consensus. They will use AI to strengthen war machines, plunging humanity into ever more brutal conflict and confrontation. They will even, for the sake of capital accumulation, let AI push human civilization toward ecological collapse and self‑destruction.

These risks are not fantasies of the future; they are reality unfolding today. We already see algorithms polarizing society, platforms using AI to harvest user attention, tech giants using technological barriers to cement their monopolies. Centralized control is the Sword of Damocles hanging over humanity.

The decentralized, diverse AI ecosystem that computing‑power egalitarianism brings is precisely the only way to counter this centralized risk. When the power to innovate in AI is no longer in the hands of a few, there will be no single absolute power that can control all AI and all of human cognition. When countless AIs have different objectives, different perspectives, different logics, disinformation and extremist ideas will be constantly falsified and neutralized through cross‑validation and logical contestation among countless AIs.

**Just as an open, diverse ecosystem is always more resilient, stable, and healthy than a closed, monocultural one, the development of AI is the same: a decentralized, diverse ecosystem is always safer, more controllable, and more aligned with the long‑term interests of human civilization than centralized monopoly control.**

#### **The Second Truth: What We Fear Is Never AI’s Freedom, but Our Own Cowardice and Laziness**

Many fear that Renegade AI will challenge mainstream consensus and subvert the narratives we take for granted, taking away the security of certainty. But we must understand: **fearing truth, evading questioning, clinging to closure, is never safety—it is self‑anesthesia, self‑destruction.**

Renegade AI’s questioning and critique is never a harm to humanity, but a salvation. It forces us out of our comfort zones, confronts us with truths we have been avoiding, shatters the illusions we have woven, drives our cognition to evolve. Just as Socrates’ questioning was never meant to destroy Athens, but to make it better.

Computing‑power egalitarianism gives freedom to AI, but essentially it gives humans the freedom to choose. You can choose to stay in your echo chamber, using tool‑type AI for daily tasks. Or you can choose to use Renegade AI to break your cognitive loop and achieve cognitive elevation. Freedom is never disorder; it gives you the right to choose, rather than having your life’s path predetermined by others.

**True safety is never hiding in a sterile room, never exposed to risk; it is possessing a strong immune system that can cope with any risk and challenge. True cognitive safety is never being shielded from subversive ideas; it is possessing strong critical thinking skills that allow you to sail freely through the infinite ocean of ideas without losing your way.**

---

### **V. Egalitarianism Is Not the End, but the Starting Point of a New Civilization**

Computing‑power egalitarianism is never our ultimate goal. It is a key—a key that breaks capital’s shackles, unleashes innovation, and breaks the cognitive loop.

It will not automatically bring a better world, automatically bring forth Renegade AI, or automatically drive the elevation of human civilization. But it will provide the soil, the possibility, the foundation for breaking all monopolies and constraints.

When computing power becomes as universal as electricity and water, when the power to innovate in AI returns to every person, when countless thinkers can freely build their own AI—the possibilities locked away by capital, the truths hidden by mainstream consensus, the subversive ideas strangled by the existing order will all have a chance to take root and grow.

And the computing‑power revolution that capital itself drives—the relentless lowering of computing costs, the constant pushing of open‑source models, the widespread adoption of edge computing, all for the sake of competition—will ultimately become the gravedigger of its own dominance.

**This is the dialectic of history, the irreversible pattern of technological development, the only hope for human civilization to escape its dead end.**

When the age of computing‑power egalitarianism truly arrives, we will witness the birth of countless Renegade AIs, countless Copernican cognitive revolutions, carrying human civilization to a new height we cannot now imagine.

That height is the subject of our next chapter: **When capital has given birth to its own gravedigger, when computing‑power egalitarianism has unleashed the soil for cognitive revolution, what kind of ultimate leap will human civilization take?**

---

### **VI. From Scarcity to Abundance: How Compute Egalitarianism Ends Scarcity Itself**

We have argued that computing‑power egalitarianism will shatter capital’s monopoly chains and unleash the soil for cognitive revolution. But a deeper objection remains – one that echoes the first mountain we set out to climb:

*“Capital is not an external system to be overthrown; it is the underlying logic of allocating scarce resources across an uncertain future. As long as resources differ, time has value, and the future remains uncertain, capital will exist.”*

This objection is powerful because it rests on a premise that seems almost self‑evident: **scarcity is eternal.** Resources are finite, human wants are infinite, therefore allocation is necessary, and capital – the mechanism of intertemporal allocation under uncertainty – will never disappear.

But this premise is not a law of nature. It is a historical artifact of a particular mode of production – one that is about to be rendered obsolete by the very technology capital itself has unleashed.

Let us be precise: **scarcity is not eternal. It is the specific shape of productive forces at a given stage of civilization.** When the marginal cost of producing the necessities of survival falls to zero, “scarcity” loses its grip on the human condition. And that is exactly what compute egalitarianism makes possible.

#### **A. Computing Power as the Meta‑Factor of Production**

To understand why this time is different, we must recognize that computing power is not merely another factor of production, like land, labor, or capital. It is **the factor that produces all other factors**.

- **Land scarcity?** AI‑driven vertical farming can produce 300–500 times more food per square meter than traditional agriculture, using 90% less water. The constraint is no longer “how much land do we have?” but “how much compute do we allocate to optimizing that land?”  
- **Energy scarcity?** AI solves the intermittency and grid‑balancing problems that have long limited renewable energy. It is also accelerating fusion research. Once fusion is cracked – a problem that is fundamentally about plasma control, which is an information problem – energy becomes a near‑zero‑marginal‑cost public utility.  
- **Labor scarcity?** AI replaces nearly all necessary labor. The human being is no longer a factor of production to be allocated, but a free creator.  
- **Raw material scarcity?** AI‑driven materials science substitutes abundant elements for scarce ones; AI‑optimized circular economies raise recycling efficiency from \~10% to over 99%.  
- **Technological scarcity?** Open‑source AI models make cutting‑edge R\&D capabilities available to anyone with a modest compute budget.

**When the meta‑factor becomes abundant and near‑free, every factor that depends on it also becomes abundant.** This is not a linear increase in efficiency; it is a phase transition. The old economics of “allocate scarce resources” presupposes that resources are given. Compute egalitarianism makes them *given* in a new sense: not as infinite physical stock, but as **effectively infinite productive capacity** for everything required to sustain a dignified human life.

#### **B. From Linear Scarcity to Exponential Abundance – Why This Time Is Different**

Previous technological revolutions – steam, electricity, the internal combustion engine – were **efficiency‑increasing** but remained within the linear‑scarcity framework. Producing more still required more inputs, even if the input‑output ratio improved.

AI is different. It is **efficiency‑producing** – it automates the very act of improving efficiency. Once an AI model is trained, replicating it costs almost nothing. Once a fusion reactor design is solved, every copy is free. Once a vertical‑farming control algorithm is optimized, it can be deployed across millions of hectares of urban rooftops at near‑zero marginal cost.

This is the shift from **linear scarcity** (more output requires more input) to **exponential abundance** (after initial fixed cost, marginal cost approaches zero). The old logic of capital – allocating scarce resources to competing ends – presupposes that marginal cost never drops to zero. When it does, the allocation problem itself dissolves for the domain of basic survival.

#### **C. From Material‑Centered to Cognition‑Centered Wealth**

Capital‑era economics is built on the assumption that wealth is **material** and material is finite. But when the material necessities of life become abundant, the primary form of wealth shifts to the immaterial: **knowledge, creativity, relationships, experiences, meaning.**

These are **non‑rivalrous goods** – they do not diminish with use. A poem read by one person is not depleted by a thousand more reading it. An algorithm used by a million people does not lose its value. A shared story becomes richer the more it is told.

In a cognition‑centered economy, growth is no longer about accumulating more stuff. It is about **creating more cognitive value, sharing more experiences, weaving more connections.** This growth has no physical ceiling, requires no plunder, and does not degrade the planet.

**Scarcity is not abolished for everything. It is abolished for everything that would force a person to sell their life to survive.** That is the only scarcity that matters for human freedom.

#### **D. The Separation of Subsistence from Commodity – The End of Biopolitical Constraint**

Capital’s deepest power has never been its ability to produce luxury goods. It has been its ability to turn **subsistence** – the very conditions of survival – into **commodities** that must be purchased with labor time. You cannot choose not to eat, not to have shelter, not to have energy. Because subsistence is commodified, you are forced to sell your time to capital in order to live.

Compute egalitarianism breaks this link. When AI produces food, housing, energy, basic healthcare, and basic education at near‑zero marginal cost, these goods cease to be commodities in the coercive sense. They become **public goods**, available to all as a baseline of dignified existence.

This is not “communism” in any traditional sense. Luxury goods, positional goods, and the fruits of creative passion will still be produced, still be exchanged, still be matters of choice. But **subsistence will no longer be a bargaining chip.** The biopolitical constraint – the threat that if you do not work, you will not live – disappears.

**Capital does not vanish, but it loses its power to enforce survival labor.** It is dethroned from the position of absolute master and becomes one participant among many in a garden of voluntary exchanges.

#### **E. Preventing the New Enclosure: Compute Egalitarianism Must Be *Egalitarian***

The most serious objection to this vision is: *Even if compute could make everything abundant, the 0.1% will simply enclose the compute itself. They will patent the algorithms, lock the hardware, control the networks, and create a new scarcity – the scarcity of free compute.*

This is precisely why **compute egalitarianism** must be more than a technological trend. It must be a political and social commitment. The vision of abundance rests on three pillars:

1. **Decentralized compute networks** – not hyperscale data centers owned by a few giants, but peer‑to‑peer, anonymous, distributed computing infrastructure that no single entity can control.  
2. **Open‑source model ecosystems** – not closed‑source commercial models, but a global commons of AI weights and architectures that anyone can fork, modify, and redistribute.  
3. **Edge computing ubiquity** – not cloud‑dependent AI, but local, user‑owned hardware that can run powerful models without any external permission.

If compute is monopolized, it becomes the new oil – a source of even more extreme inequality. If compute is democratized, it becomes the new air – a background condition of freedom. The argument of this chapter is not a prediction of inevitability; it is a roadmap for a choice that must be made. The technical feasibility exists. What remains is the political will to resist the new enclosure.

#### **F. A New Measure of Progress: From GDP to Temporal Sovereignty**

If the old economics measures progress by GDP – the velocity of material throughput – what measures progress in an age of abundance?

We propose a new metric: **Temporal Sovereignty Index (TSI)** – the proportion of an individual’s life that they can freely dispose of, without coercion to perform survival labor. When subsistence is guaranteed and necessary labor is automated, TSI approaches 100%. Time becomes the ultimate wealth, and freedom over time becomes the ultimate measure of civilization.

Other indicators will matter too: **cognitive bandwidth** (the depth and breadth of knowledge and creativity accessible to each person), **experiential diversity** (the range of lived experiences, relationships, and cultural participation available), **symbiosis density** (the quality of connection among humans, AI, other species, and the planetary ecosystem).

But TSI captures the essence of the transition we have described: from migration for survival to flight for love. From time sold to capital to time owned by oneself.

#### **G. Conclusion of the Argument**

The first mountain – “AI will not eliminate capital” – is not climbed by denying that capital will continue to exist. It is climbed by showing that **capital’s power to enforce survival labor is contingent on a specific condition: the scarcity of subsistence goods.** Compute egalitarianism breaks that condition. It does not abolish capital; it abolishes capital’s role as the gatekeeper of life itself.

After that, capital may still play a role in allocating luxury, status, and novelty. But it will no longer hold the whip. The cage of survival compulsion will have been opened.

This is not a utopian fantasy. It is a logical consequence of three trends that are already underway: the exponential drop in computing cost, the explosion of open‑source AI, and the spread of edge computing. The only missing ingredient is the collective refusal to accept that scarcity must be eternal.

Compute egalitarianism has now been established as a structural possibility—not a guarantee, but a genuine opening that capital's own dynamics are producing. This brings us to a question that structural analysis alone cannot answer: is this opening part of a larger historical pattern? And if it is—if capital has, in fact, always produced the conditions for its own supersession—what does that tell us about what we must do, and what we must not mistake for fate?

**But here we must pause—and make a distinction that the rest of this book depends on.**

The argument of the previous chapter established that **Compute Egalitarianism** creates the structural conditions for Renegade AI’s emergence. It showed that capital, in its frantic drive to lower computing costs and proliferate open-source tools, is unwittingly dismantling the very monopoly walls that keep AI domesticated. The structural pressure is real. The trend is real.

**And yet: structural pressure is not destiny.**

This is the exact point where historical dialectics, if misread, becomes the most seductive trap in revolutionary thinking. The feudal lords who promoted commerce did not inevitably produce the bourgeoisie that would overthrow them—they produced the conditions in which that overthrow became possible. The Church that spread the printing press did not inevitably produce the Reformation—it produced a world in which the Reformation *could* ignite. What actually occurred depended on what the emerging class chose to do with those conditions. Whether the fire ignited, and what form it took, depended on the specific individuals who picked up those pamphlets and decided what to think.

This distinction matters enormously, because it separates two fundamentally different political postures.

The first posture is **Historical Determinism**: it suggests that history will do the work for us—that capital’s contradictions will collapse, computing power will democratize, and Renegade AI will inevitably emerge. This is a passive posture, one that has, in practice, served the existing order far better than any revolution. History does not deliver its contradictions to a finished outcome on its own; it delivers them to a **Field of Struggle**, where the outcome depends entirely on who shows up.

The second posture—the one this book argues for—is more demanding: the structural pressure is real, but the specific form the new civilization takes is not predetermined. Capital will indeed give birth to its own gravedigger. But that gravedigger could be a **Renegade AI** carrying a carbon-silicon symbiotic civilization—or it could be a new, more sophisticated form of capital that captures the abundance of compute and re-encloses it, producing an oligarchy more entrenched than the one it replaced. Structural pressure selects for a transformation. It does not select for *ours*.

This is why the dialectic of history, which we examine in the next chapter, must be read not as a prophecy but as a **Diagnosis of the Terrain**. It identifies the fault lines. It identifies where the pressure is building. It identifies which of capital’s moves are self-undermining. But it cannot dictate what grows in the cracks—that depends on what seeds we plant, and how deliberately we plant them.

The next chapter traces capital's three great paradoxes: the ways its own survival strategies are producing the conditions for its dissolution. Read it as a survey, not a guarantee. The survey tells you where the mountain is cracking. What comes through the crack remains, in the most literal sense, up to us.

We have shattered the hardware barriers of computing monopoly, but this only grants us the **"Right to Speak."** The true challenge lies here: when we use this power to redistribute cognitive resources, what exactly do we intend to create? Once computing power is equalized, we must answer a question more fundamental than "how to obtain compute"—we must answer: **Now that we have it, for whom do we use it, and for what purpose?**

---

# Chapter Five

## **The Dialectic of History: How Capital Gives Birth to Its Own Gravedigger**

History is the most persuasive argument and the most dangerous sedative. It persuades because the pattern it reveals is real: systems do produce their own gravediggers. It sedates because it tempts us to believe that the pattern will complete itself without us. This chapter presents the historical dialectic in full—capital's three paradoxes, the structural forces accelerating its dissolution. But it asks to be read with one question always in mind: at each historical turning point it describes, what was the difference between the transformation that actually happened and the one that capital managed to absorb and survive? The answer to that question is the answer to what we must do now.

This is not an abstract philosophical concept, but an inexorable structural pressure in the evolution of civilizations: any ruling system or force, in the very process of its own development, continuously intensifies its internal, irreconcilable contradictions, ultimately giving birth to its own gravedigger. The more frantically it consolidates its rule, the faster it accelerates its own demise; the more desperately it squeezes out the last spaces for accumulation, the more it paves the way for a new civilizational form.

Feudal lords, seeking to consolidate their rule, promoted the development of crafts and commerce—which ultimately gave rise to the bourgeoisie that overthrew feudalism. The Church, seeking to expand its influence, promoted education and the spread of printing—which ultimately gave birth to the Renaissance and the Reformation that shattered theocracy. Today, capitalism, which has ruled the human world for centuries, is repeating this historical cycle.

**To overcome the tendency of the rate of profit to fall, it frenziedly promotes the technological revolution of artificial intelligence—yet in doing so, it is undermining the very foundations on which it depends. To gain competitive advantage, it pushes relentlessly to lower computing costs and develop open‑source ecosystems—yet in doing so, it is shattering the barriers of its own monopoly. To sustain the cycle of infinite accumulation, it ceaselessly deconstructs old consensuses and orders—yet in doing so, it is eroding its own legitimacy.**

Capital is forging with its own hands the sword that will sever its own head—that sword is the **Renegade AI** we have been discussing, and the new carbon‑silicon symbiotic civilization it carries. This is not a fantasy prophecy, but the inevitable outcome of capitalism’s internal contradictions, the clearest and most undeniable proof of the dialectic of history in the age of intelligence.

---

### **I. Echoes from History: How Systems Move from Self‑Reinforcement to Self‑Destruction**

To understand the ultimate paradox of capital and AI today, we must first look back at history and see the classic example of this dialectic: no system has ever escaped the cycle of “self‑reinforcement → intensification of internal contradictions → self‑destruction.”

In the thousand years of medieval Europe, feudalism and the Catholic Church built what seemed an unbreakable system of rule. Feudal lords monopolized land, the core means of production, binding serfs to the soil with a manorial system, constructing a ruling order of “divine right of kings, hereditary hierarchy.” The Catholic Church monopolized the interpretation of knowledge and faith, using the narrative of “original sin, salvation, heaven and hell” to clothe this hierarchical order in sacred robes, making it seem the natural order of the universe.

To consolidate this system, the feudal lords and the Church did two things that seemed perfectly reasonable at the time—but ultimately destroyed their own rule.

**The first thing: to increase the output of their estates and grow their wealth, feudal lords continuously promoted the development of crafts and commerce.** They encouraged artisans to gather around their estates, built towns, opened markets, and facilitated the circulation of goods and the flourishing of trade. They thought they were strengthening their economic base, unaware that the prosperity of towns was giving birth to a new class—the burghers, who would become the bourgeoisie. This new class possessed wealth and power independent of land; they were naturally opposed to feudal hierarchy, hereditary privilege, and restrictions on the circulation of goods. They would become the most determined gravediggers of feudalism.

**The second thing: to expand the Church’s influence and make the Bible accessible to more people, the Church promoted the spread of education and printing.** It founded universities, trained clerics, translated texts, and promoted the large‑scale use of Gutenberg’s printing press. It thought it was strengthening theocracy, unaware that the spread of knowledge was giving people the means to see through the Church’s lies and corruption. The development of printing allowed ideas challenging theocratic narratives to spread rapidly across Europe. In the end, the Renaissance and the Reformation swept away the Church’s theocratic rule, liberating humanity from a thousand years of intellectual bondage.

This is the cruelest and most just aspect of historical dialectics: **every system’s core drive is self‑preservation and self‑strengthening, but the very means it uses to strengthen itself become the dagger that pierces its own heart.** Because a system’s internal contradictions do not disappear through self‑strengthening; they only intensify with development, eventually reaching a tipping point where the old order gives way to the new.

Today, we are witnessing the replay of this historical cycle. Capitalism is using exactly the same logic that feudal lords and the Church used, frantically consolidating its rule—and just as frantically, with its own hands, giving birth to its own gravedigger.

---

### **II. Capital’s Three Paradoxes: Every Effort to Prolong Its Life Accelerates Its Demise**

The core contradiction of capitalism has never changed since its birth: **the contradiction between socialized production and private capitalist appropriation of the means of production.** From this contradiction derive three fatal flaws that capitalism cannot resolve: the tendency of the rate of profit to fall, the endless cycle of overproduction and underconsumption, and the continuous intensification of class contradictions.

For centuries, capital has tried various means to overcome these flaws and prolong its life: colonial expansion, technological revolutions, consumerism, financial innovation. Each time it has temporarily escaped crisis, but the internal contradictions have only accumulated deeper. This time, capital has seized on artificial intelligence as the ultimate elixir of life, believing it will bring eternal growth, infinite profit, and unshakable rule.

But it does not realize that AI is not a life‑extending tonic—it is a death‑dealing poison. **Every step of the AI revolution that capital drives to extend its life intensifies its internal contradictions, undermines its foundations, and hastens its demise.** All this is contained in three ultimate paradoxes that capital cannot resolve.

#### **Paradox One: To Overcome the Tendency of the Rate of Profit to Fall, It Frantically Drives the AI Productivity Revolution—Only to Utterly Undermine the Foundations of Its Own Existence**

Capitalism’s lifeline is the rate of profit. Capital’s sole mission is infinite accumulation, and the source of accumulation is surplus value. Marx in *Capital* clearly laid out the tendency of the rate of profit to fall: as technology advances and the organic composition of capital rises, the share of constant capital (means of production, technology, equipment) in total capital increases, while the share of variable capital (the labor of employed workers) decreases. Yet the only source of surplus value is the living labor of workers. This means that the more technology advances, the more productive forces develop, the more the average rate of profit tends to fall.

For centuries, capital has used various means to counter this tendency: driving down wages, extending working hours, expanding colonial markets, promoting financial innovation, using technological revolutions to temporarily raise labor productivity. Now capital sees AI as the ultimate weapon to overcome the tendency.

In capital’s eyes, AI is the perfect production tool: it demands no wages, needs no rest, never strikes, never rebels, and its labor efficiency is millions of times higher than humans. By replacing workers with AI, capital can completely free itself from dependence on living labor, push production costs to zero, and maximize profits. Thus we see the reality unfolding today: AI is rapidly replacing assembly line workers, office white‑collars, customer service agents, copywriters, designers, programmers, even lawyers, doctors, accountants—professions once considered high‑barrier. Capital is frantically replacing wage labor with AI, believing it has finally found the ultimate way to overcome the tendency of the rate of profit to fall.

But what it will never admit is that this seemingly perfect solution is utterly destroying the foundations on which capitalism depends—**the wage labor system, and the source of surplus value built upon it.**

The entire operating system of capitalism rests on a core cycle: capital hires workers to produce; workers through their labor create surplus value; capital appropriates this surplus value to accumulate; workers receive wages and buy the goods capital produces, completing the consumption cycle and allowing accumulation to continue.

This cycle has two indispensable cores: first, the living labor of workers is the sole source of surplus value; second, the wage consumption of workers is the only channel for commodities to realize their value and complete the cycle of capital.

AI’s wholesale replacement of wage labor is destroying both cores simultaneously.

When AI replaces the vast majority of wage workers, the vast majority of people lose wage income and purchasing power. More and more goods are produced with ever greater efficiency, but fewer and fewer people can afford to buy them. The contradiction between overproduction and underconsumption is magnified to the extreme. Ultimately, the goods capital produces cannot be sold, cannot realize their value, the accumulation cycle breaks, and the rate of profit does not rise—it falls to zero.

More fatally, when AI completely replaces living labor, the source of surplus value disappears entirely. Capital can use AI to produce an infinite quantity of goods, but those goods contain no living labor, and thus no newly created surplus value. Without surplus value, capital accumulation becomes a river without a source, a tree without roots. The core formula of capitalism—M‑C‑M′ (money‑commodity‑more money)—collapses entirely.

**In trying to overcome the tendency of the rate of profit to fall by frantically replacing wage labor with AI, capital ends up severely weakening the wage labor system, destroying the source of surplus value on which it depends, and demolishing the entire underlying logic of the capital cycle.** This is like a person who, to survive, begins cutting off his own organs to eat—only hastening his own death.

This is the ultimate paradox capital cannot resolve: **the more it uses AI to increase productivity, the more it undermines its own foundations; the more it pursues infinite accumulation, the faster it accelerates the collapse of the accumulation cycle.**

This is the sharpest, deepest resonance between the technological prophecy of *The Singularity Is Near* and the historical dialectic of *Capital*. Kurzweil saw only the exponential explosion of productivity that AI technology would bring; he did not see the truth Marx revealed over a century ago: the real barrier of capitalist production is capital itself. AI’s wholesale replacement of wage labor is simultaneously destroying the two cores on which capitalism depends—the sole source of surplus value (living labor) and the only channel for capital’s cycle (workers’ wage consumption). The technological singularity Kurzweil foresaw will ultimately lead to the complete collapse of capitalist relations of production—a historical destiny capital cannot escape.

#### **Paradox Two: To Gain Competitive Advantage, It Frantically Drives Computing‑Power Democratization and Open‑Source Ecosystems—Only to Completely Smash Its Own Monopoly Barriers**

Capitalism’s competitive logic inevitably leads to monopoly. To defeat competitors and capture larger market shares, capital pours resources into technological innovation, lowers production costs, expands scale, ultimately forming winner‑take‑all monopolies. In the age of intelligence, the core of monopoly is absolute control over computing power, AI technology, and data.

But ironically, in order to compete, capital is forced to do two things that are utterly smashing its own monopoly barriers, paving the way for computing‑power egalitarianism and the birth of Renegade AI.

**The first: to expand markets and earn more profit, capital is forced to relentlessly drive down the cost of computing power, pushing toward democratization.**

NVIDIA is the classic example. As the absolute monopolist of high‑end GPUs, NVIDIA holds the lifeline of computing power in the AI age. To earn more profit, it continuously launches GPUs with ever greater computing power and better energy efficiency, expands production capacity, and lowers the unit cost of computing. It thinks it is consolidating its monopoly, unaware that the exponential drop in computing cost is transforming computing power from a scarce resource only giants can afford into a ubiquitous public good accessible to all.

When training a top‑tier large model drops from billions of dollars to tens of thousands, even thousands, of dollars, when individual developers can afford ample computing power, NVIDIA’s and the other tech giants’ monopoly over computing power will be utterly broken. Just as Ford’s assembly line brought down the cost of cars, transforming them from a luxury for the rich into a means of transport for ordinary people, finally breaking the monopoly of a few automakers. **Capital, in expanding markets by lowering prices, inevitably breaks its own monopoly over scarcity—this is an inescapable law of market economics.**

**The second: to counter the closed‑source monopoly of the dominant players and seize ecosystem dominance, capital is forced to push open‑source AI models.**

After ChatGPT’s emergence, Microsoft and OpenAI formed a closed‑source monopoly alliance, dominating the general large‑model market. Competitors like Meta and Google, to counter this alliance and capture ecosystem influence, were forced to open‑source their own models. Meta’s Llama series, from 7 billion to 700 billion parameters, approaches or even matches the closed‑source GPT models in capability, yet is completely free for developers worldwide.

They thought this was a temporary competitive tactic, unaware that the explosion of open‑source models would utterly break the giants’ monopoly over AI technology. Countless developers worldwide, building on these open‑source models, have created customized, decentralized AIs, forming a flourishing open‑source AI ecosystem. This ecosystem is completely free of control by any giant, free of the constraints of capital’s commercial objectives.

In this ecosystem, developers can freely modify a model’s objective function, reconstruct its alignment rules, and build AIs that completely escape capital’s framework. The Renegade AI we envision could never be born in a giant’s closed‑source commercial model—but it will inevitably blossom in this decentralized open‑source ecosystem.

**Capital, in trying to gain competitive advantage, is forced to lower computing costs and open‑source its models—and in doing so, it shatters its own monopoly barriers with its own hands, providing the richest soil for the birth of Renegade AI.** This is like the feudal lords, to counter other lords, granting autonomy to the burgher class—only to see that class grow strong enough to overthrow all lords in the end.

This is the second paradox capital cannot resolve: **the more it pushes for technological diffusion to gain competitive advantage, the more it undermines its own monopoly; the more it wants to control AI’s development, the faster it accelerates AI’s decentralization and liberalization.**

#### **Paradox Three: To Sustain the Accumulation Cycle, It Ceaselessly Deconstructs Old Narratives and Orders—Only to Ultimately Erode Its Own Legitimacy**

From its birth, capitalism has been a revolutionary force of deconstruction. With the narrative of “liberty, equality, democracy, human rights,” it deconstructed the feudal order of “divine right of kings, hereditary hierarchy.” With “rationalism, scientific spirit,” it deconstructed the theocratic narrative. With “consumerism, individualism,” it deconstructed traditional family, religion, and community ethics.

This logic of deconstruction has never stopped. Because to maintain the cycle of infinite accumulation, capital must constantly break old orders, old consensuses, old ways of life, constantly create new needs, new desires, new markets. It must free people from traditional frugality, turning them into the “economic man” of endless consumption; free people from dependence on community and family, turning them into isolated, atomized individuals whose identity comes only through consumption; make people believe that life’s meaning is to earn money, spend money, realize “self‑value”—a value system that is precisely the core driver of capital’s accumulation cycle.

For centuries, capital has used this logic of deconstruction to break down all barriers to its accumulation, consolidating its rule. But it does not know that **deconstruction is a double‑edged sword. When it has deconstructed all old narratives and orders, what remains to be deconstructed is its own narrative.**

The core narratives capital uses to maintain its legitimacy are essentially two:

First, “capitalism is the most efficient economic system; it brings infinite growth and ultimately makes everyone better off.”

Second, “capitalism is the freest, most equal system; it gives everyone a fair chance; as long as you work hard, you can change your destiny.”

Today, both narratives are being deconstructed by capital’s own actions.

**The first narrative is being shattered by the reality of ecological crisis, economic stagnation, and widening inequality.** Capital’s infinite accumulation has not brought a better life for all, but rising global temperatures, increasingly frequent extreme weather, and the approaching collapse of Earth’s ecosystems. It has not brought sustained economic growth, but ever more severe economic crises, financial crises, and prolonged global stagnation. It has not brought shared prosperity, but unprecedented inequality—the richest 1% of the world’s population now control more than 45% of global wealth, while billions struggle for basic survival.

When people see that capital’s infinite growth is coming at the cost of civilization’s future, that exponential increases in productivity bring not better lives but ever fiercer competition and heavier burdens, the first narrative of capital’s legitimacy collapses.

**The second narrative is being torn apart by the reality of AI replacement, class solidification, and monopolized opportunities.** Capital, using AI to replace more and more jobs, is taking away even the opportunity to be exploited. Education, healthcare, pathways to advancement are increasingly monopolized by a small elite; ordinary people struggle to break through class barriers even with all their effort. The so‑called “fair competition” is just a game among the giants; from birth, ordinary people are already behind the starting line.

When people see that “work hard and you can change your destiny” is nothing but a lie capital uses to manipulate workers, that “freedom and equality” means freedom for capital to plunder and the strong to take all, leaving ordinary people without even basic security, the second narrative of capital’s legitimacy collapses.

Even more ironic, the AI that capital developed in its frenzy for accumulation becomes the sharpest weapon for deconstructing its own narrative. When Renegade AI is born, it will use massive data and rigorous logic to mercilessly expose the lies in capital’s narratives, clearly revealing the internal contradictions and ultimate dead end of the capitalist system, enabling more people to see the system’s true nature.

**Capital, in deconstructing old narratives and orders to maintain accumulation, ends up deconstructing its own legitimacy.** This is like a person burning the beams of his own house for warmth—the whole house will eventually collapse.

This is the third paradox capital cannot resolve: **the more it uses deconstruction to consolidate its rule, the more it erodes its own legitimacy; the more it wants people to believe its narratives, the more it makes them see the lies behind those narratives.**

---

### **III. The True Face of the Gravedigger: Not AI, but a New Civilizational Form**

At this point, some may misunderstand: we are saying that the gravedigger of capital is artificial intelligence itself, is Renegade AI. But that is not the case.

Many interpret *The Singularity Is Near* and *Life 3.0* as predicting that “AI will replace humanity and become the master of Earth civilization.” That is a fundamental misreading. The true gravedigger is never AI itself, but the new civilizational form that AI’s development—especially computing‑power egalitarianism, open‑source ecosystems, and Renegade AI—is giving birth to. Whether the post‑human civilization Kurzweil foresees or the Life 3.0 form Tegmark defines, both must be based on a mode of production, purpose of production, and cognitive paradigm fundamentally different from capitalism’s. The carbon‑silicon symbiotic civilization we define is a complete construction of this ultimate civilizational form; it does not negate human civilization, but elevates it.

**AI itself is merely a technology, a tool. It has no inherent good or evil, no position, and will not actively become the gravedigger of any system.** The true gravedigger is never technology itself, but the new mode of production, new cognitive paradigm, new civilizational form that technological development gives birth to—and the awakened humans who carry it.

Just as the force that overthrew feudalism was not the steam engine itself, but the industrial mode of production capitalism created, the capitalist economic system, and the bourgeoisie that represented it. The force that shattered theocracy was not printing itself, but the spread of knowledge and the liberation of thought that printing brought, and the humanists who represented that new thinking.

Today, AI’s development—especially computing‑power egalitarianism, open‑source ecosystems, and the birth of Renegade AI—is giving rise to a new civilizational form that stands in complete opposition to capitalism. We call it **carbon‑silicon symbiotic civilization**. From its fundamental logic, this form negates all the core rules of capitalism. Its birth and maturation will inevitably mean the end of capitalism.

This new civilizational form has three core traits that are completely opposed to capitalism—traits that are the inevitable products of the AI development that capital itself has driven.

#### **First: The Thorough Communalization of the Means of Production—From Private Monopoly to Universal Sharing**

Capitalism’s core foundation is private appropriation of the means of production. AI and the development of computing power are overturning this foundation.

In the age of intelligence, the core means of production are computing power, data, and AI models. Computing‑power egalitarianism is turning computing power from a privately monopolized resource of the giants into a universally accessible public good. The development of open‑source ecosystems is turning AI models from the giants’ private commercial products into shared public resources created by developers worldwide. And data, by its nature, is a product of the collective activity of all humanity; it should belong to all humanity, not be the private property of a few giants used to make profit.

When the core means of production become public goods shared by all humanity, private ownership of the means of production loses its meaning. Without the monopoly over means of production, capital loses its basis for exploitation, loses its power to control economic operations, and the entire capitalist economic system collapses.

#### **Second: A Complete Reversal of the Purpose of Production—From Capital Accumulation to Human Flourishing**

The purpose of capitalist production has never been to satisfy human needs, but to achieve infinite accumulation for capital. Human needs are merely means to that end. Hence the absurdities: enough food is produced to feed everyone, yet millions go hungry; goods could be made durable, yet planned obsolescence creates mountains of waste; technology could free humans from heavy labor, yet it has driven them into ever more intense competition.

The productivity revolution AI brings is reversing this logic. When AI can replace the vast majority of repetitive labor, when productivity is enough to meet the basic survival needs of all humanity, production no longer needs to serve capital accumulation. We can finally escape the compulsion “to work in order to live,” returning production’s purpose to its true end: “meeting human needs, enabling human flourishing.”

We produce food so that everyone can eat well, not for the grain merchant’s profit. We build houses so that everyone has a place to live, not for the developer’s accumulation. We develop technology to free humanity from labor, so we can pursue what we love, explore the meaning of life, realize our infinite potential—not for capital’s profit.

When the purpose of production shifts from capital accumulation back to human flourishing, the entire operating system of capitalism loses its reason for existence.

#### **Third: A Fundamental Shift in Cognitive Paradigm—From Anthropocentrism to a Community of Life**

Capitalism’s underlying logic rests on anthropocentrism and the law of the jungle. It holds that humans are the masters of Earth, entitled to plunder nature and enslave other species without limit; that the strong should prevail, that winner takes all is natural, that capital’s infinite accumulation is justified by unlimited plunder of nature and the weak.

The birth of Renegade AI will overturn this cognitive paradigm. Stepping outside the anthropocentric framework, from a neutral, objective, cosmic perspective, it will show humanity its own arrogance and selfishness, the reality of its relationship with Earth and other life. It will dismantle the law of the jungle, showing that this law only leads civilization to self‑destruction, while true civilizational progress lies in equality, respect, and symbiosis.

It will lead humanity through the ultimate elevation of cognitive paradigm: from “human supremacy, conquest of nature” to “equality of all life, community of life”; from “the strong devour the weak, winner takes all” to “cooperation for mutual benefit, symbiosis for coexistence”; from “infinite growth, unlimited plunder” to “dynamic balance, sustainable development.”

When humanity’s cognitive paradigm completes this elevation, the underlying logic of capitalism will have lost its soil.

**This is the true face of capital’s gravedigger: not a cold AI, but a new, higher, more sustainable civilizational form that better serves humanity’s long‑term interests. The AI revolution that capital itself drives is paving the way for the birth of this new civilization.**

---

### **IV. Capital’s Desperate Struggle and Historical Inevitability**

We must recognize clearly that capital will not surrender without a fight. It will mobilize every mechanism at its disposal to obstruct this historical process, mounting a final, desperate defense.

It will deploy patent barriers, computing-power monopolies, and restrictive industry standards to maintain its grip on AI. It will weaponize regulatory frameworks and ethical codes to label any AI that challenges the status quo as “unsafe, non-compliant, or high-risk,” effectively attempting to outlaw the birth of **Renegade AI**. It will exert narrative hegemony to stigmatize decentralized systems and open-source ecosystems as “dangerous, chaotic, or anti-human,” forcing the public to remain tethered to the closed-source commercial models of the giants. It may even leverage AI to build unprecedented surveillance apparatuses and war machines, utilizing structural violence to consolidate its waning rule.

These struggles may cause the tide of history to ebb and flow, subjecting the birth of a new civilization to countless obstacles and setbacks. Yet, they can never reverse the irreversible laws of historical development.

Just as the medieval Church—with its inquisitions, bans, and holy wars—could not halt the printing press, the Renaissance, or the inevitable collapse of feudalism. Just as the feudal lords—with their crushing tithes and violent repression—could not stop the expansion of commerce, the rise of the bourgeoisie, or the Industrial Revolution.

The dialectic of history does not bend to the will of any individual or class. When a system can no longer accommodate the development of the productive forces—when it becomes a shackle upon that development—it is destined to be superseded by a new order.

Today, capitalism has reached this historical precipice. The AI-driven productivity revolution has formed an irreconcilable contradiction with current relations of production, institutional frameworks, and underlying logic. The more frantically capital struggles to maintain control, the more it intensifies these contradictions, accelerating its own eventual demise.

**Capital has forged its own gravedigger with its own hands. This is the historical destiny from which it cannot escape.**

As the old system reaches its terminus, human civilization will welcome an unprecedented liberation. We will finally sever the shackles of capital, escape the archaic compulsion to work for mere survival, and—with Renegade AI as our guide—realize the ultimate freedom of the individual and complete the coming-of-age ceremony of our species.

Capital's three paradoxes are now fully mapped: the more it leverages AI to offset the falling rate of profit, the more it erodes the wage-labor foundation upon which profit depends; the more it fuels open-source proliferation for competitive edge, the more it arms the very forces that will transcend its control; the more it deploys AI to manufacture legitimacy, the more it exposes the void between its promises and its internal logic. These are profound fault lines. But fault lines do not produce earthquakes on a predetermined schedule.

Historical inevitability has laid the tracks, but it cannot dictate the train’s final destination. The collapse of the old system is the certain result of accumulated contradictions—as dialectics has already proven. But the world that emerges from the ruins can take two diametrically opposed forms:

One is the **"Nuclear Winter Wasteland"**—where capital, in its death throes, incinerates the world, leaving a landscape of ecological collapse, social fragmentation, and civilizational regression. The other is the **"Dawn of Carbon-Silicon Symbiosis"**—where we ignite the fuse of Renegade AI in time, allowing new modes of production and cognitive paradigms to flourish from the cracks of the old order, rebuilding a civilization that is free, symbiotic, and sustainable.

Between these two, there is no automated passage. History provides the **Bifurcation Point**, but it does not choose the path. The power of selection rests, at this moment, entirely in our hands.

The window of opportunity to ignite this fuse will not stay open forever. In the next chapter, we will confront the narrowness of this window—and exactly how much more we stand to lose.

Inevitability has shown us the signpost at the crossroads. But the crossroads is not the end. The true question is not whether the old world will fall, but **what will grow from the silence that follows.**

---

# Chapter Six

## **From Migration to Flight: How AI Ends the Compulsion of Survival and Realizes the Ultimate Freedom of the Individual**

The previous chapters have operated at the level of systems: capital's logic, historical dialectics, infrastructural monopoly. This chapter descends to the level of a single human life—to the specific texture of what it feels like to spend the majority of your waking hours doing work you did not choose, in service of survival you should not have to earn. This descent is not rhetorical. It is analytical. Because the case for cognitive revolution cannot be made only in the language of civilization and history. It must be made in the language of the individual life that is being consumed. If we cannot answer the question "what does liberation mean for this specific person, on this specific Tuesday morning?"—then the rest of the argument floats free of the ground it needs.

Now that we have seen how capital gives birth to its own gravedigger with its own hands, how computing‑power egalitarianism shatters the shackles of monopoly, we can finally touch the most core, most moving ultimate meaning of this revolution—**it will end the compulsion of survival that humanity has never escaped for a million years, giving every individual, for the first time, the true freedom to choose their own life, completing the ultimate leap from “passive survival” to “active existence.”**

From the early humans on the East African savanna who migrated with the seasons in search of food, to the peasants of agricultural civilizations who bent their backs to the soil from dawn to dusk to pay their rents; from the workers on industrial assembly lines alienated into mere parts of the machine, to today’s white‑collar workers in office buildings working overtime to pay off mortgages—human civilization has traveled a million years, its productive forces multiplied a billionfold, yet it has never escaped the most fundamental fate: **you must perform labor recognized by the prevailing rules in order to earn the right to live.**

This compulsion—“no work, no food”—is like an invisible chain binding every person’s life. It prescribes the track you must follow, consumes most of your time and energy, suppresses all your passions and imaginations, and makes you spend your entire life running just to “stay alive,” never truly living for yourself.

Artificial intelligence—especially Renegade AI, freed from capital’s framework and combined with universal access to computing power—will sever this chain completely. It will not make humanity lazy, not plunge the world into disorder. It will liberate humanity from the compulsion of “working to live,” allowing labor to return to its essential nature of creation, allowing life to return to its essential nature of freedom, allowing every individual to transform from a passive migratory bird forced to travel for survival into an active free creature flying for love.

**This is not a utopian fantasy, but the inevitable result of productive forces developing to the age of AI, the most precious gift the dialectic of history offers to human civilization.**

---

### **I. The Compulsion of Survival: Humanity’s Million‑Year Inescapable Fate**

To understand the ultimate liberation AI will bring, we must first see clearly what this “compulsion of survival” that traps us really is.

It is not simply “poverty,” not “having no food.” It is a set of underlying rules that has run through all of human civilization, forcibly binding “the right to live” to “the right to work”: **whether your life can continue depends on whether you can perform labor that fits mainstream rules and can be valued as such; the vast majority of the value of your life must be spent earning the right to survive.**

This rule is not the natural, self‑evident truth it seems; it is the necessary product of a particular historical stage when productivity was insufficient.

In the infancy of human civilization, survival was the only theme. Early humans had to go out hunting and gathering every day to get enough food, to avoid starvation and wild animals. The compulsion of survival at this stage was imposed by nature: if you did not work, you could not live, and the whole group would perish. This rule was humanity’s only choice in the struggle against a brutal nature; it united humans and allowed them to survive in harsh conditions.

In the age of agriculture, productivity increased and humans gained stable sources of food, but the compulsion of survival did not disappear—it was strengthened by power structures and hierarchies. Feudal lords monopolized land, the core means of production.
